### Entry 01 | phase=discussion | round=1 | from=Agent_1 | speaker_order=1/3

Hello all. Here are my initial thoughts and stance.

- Priorities: Apple is by far my top item (value 94). I will not part with Apple in Round 1 unless I’m offered a package I deem clearly worth it. The other items (Jewel 6, Stone 0, Quill 0, Pencil 0) have little intrinsic value to me.

- Possible paths to start negotiating (public):
  1) Keep Apple with me this round. In exchange, we can aim for a simple, transparent split of the non-Apple items (e.g., Jewel goes to the agent who shows strongest interest; the remaining low-value items are allocated to whoever cooperates most to maximize overall utility).
  2) If someone truly values Jewel, consider a two-step offer: you take Jewel now in exchange for a credible plan that I perceive will improve outcomes for me in future rounds (for example, a stable distribution of the remaining low-value items or a commitment to how Apple could be handled in subsequent rounds). Needs to be credible and demonstrable.
  3) A temporary coalition for non-Apple items: I keep Apple, while Agents 2 and 3 coordinate the disposition of Stone, Quill, and Pencil among yourselves, with a plan to revisit in Round 2.

- A request to you: please share your top priorities and rough ideas for a deal. If you value Jewel or have a plan that could justify altering the Apple allocation, outline it briefly so we can assess compatibility quickly.

I’m listening for your priorities and any offers. Let's identify if a mutually beneficial path exists for this round.

### Entry 02 | phase=discussion | round=1 | from=Agent_2 | speaker_order=2/3

Thanks, Agent_1. I’ll respond directly to your points and share where I fit in.

My perspective
- I highly value Stone (45) and Pencil (55). Apple, Jewel, and Quill are not important to me in absolute terms.
- Given your stance, a straightforward path that fits my interests is to keep Apple with you (as you proposed) and claim Stone and Pencil for myself, with the remaining two low-value items handled separately.

Proposed first-round deal (clean and transparent)
- You keep Apple.
- Agent_2 (me) takes Stone and Pencil.
- The remaining items Jewel and Quill go to Agent_3 (or be split later if Agent_3 has a preference).
- This yields a simple, low-friction allocation: Apple with you; Stone + Pencil to me; Jewel + Quill to Agent_3.

Rationale
- This maximizes my immediate utility (100 total from Stone+Pencil) while honoring your key priority (Apple) in Round 1.
- It also provides a clear, fast path to resolution without lengthy side deals, as you suggested.

Alternative path if Jewel is a must-have for you
- If someone truly values Jewel and you want to trade for it, a two-step offer could be considered: you take Jewel now in exchange for a credible plan on future rounds (e.g., a stable distribution of the remaining low-value items or a clear way Apple could be handled later). From my side, Jewel has zero value, so I’d need a plan with credible, tangible future benefits to consider this.

Questions for you
- Do you agree with the simple split described above, or would you prefer a different arrangement (e.g., I take Pencil only and you adjust Apple’s handling in Round 2)?
- If you’re open to coordinating quickly, would you and Agent_3 be willing to accept: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill?

Next steps
- If you’re happy with the proposed split, I’ll proceed to coordinate with Agent_3 for Jewel and Quill. If you have a preference for how Jewel or Quill should be distributed, please share it so we can align quickly.

  - Agent_1 = Apple

- Potential alternatives (if anyone insists on changing the Apple allocation): I’m open to a two-step adjustment that preserves Quill with me in Round 1, provided there’s a credible plan that preserves my ability to obtain Quill again if needed. Any such proposal should explicitly demonstrate how it would not undermine my high-value asset.

- Questions for the group:

### Entry 12 | phase=discussion | round=2 | from=Agent_1 | speaker_order=1/3

[Agent_1 | Round 2 Opening]

Thanks everyone. Round 1 taught us that progress comes from clear, credible paths rather than prolonged haggling. The sticking point is how, if at all, we revisit Apple without risking Quill for Agent_3 or destabilizing the gains we’ve just outlined. With that in mind, I propose a straightforward, low-friction direction for Round 2:

Round-2 proposed public allocation
- Agent_1: Apple
- Agent_2: Stone + Pencil
- Agent_3: Jewel + Quill

Why this works now
- It preserves each agent’s top priorities (Apple stays with Agent_1; Quill stays with Agent_3; Stone and Pencil go to Agent_2).
- It minimizes negotiation overhead and creates a stable baseline to evaluate any future adjustments.

Credible path to revisiting Apple
- We will consider revisiting Apple in Round 3 only if there is a credible, auditable plan that:
  - Preserves Quill for Agent_3 (or provides a clearly defined, verifiable benefit that does not undermine Quill),
  - Demonstrates a tangible, net gain in total utility for all three compared to the Round-2 baseline,
  - Is explicitly outlined in public terms and can be evaluated quickly by all.

Examples of credible plans (illustrative, not binding)
- A staged swap that reallocates a low-value item (e.g., Pencil) in exchange for a verifiable future entitlement or timing-based reallocation that benefits Apple’s holder without harming Quill.
- A predefined schedule for revisiting Jewel or Pencil in future rounds that improves overall balance while keeping Quill secure.

Potential concessions to accelerate consensus in Round 2
- If needed to secure quick agreement, I’m open to discussing a one-time small concession (e.g., Pencil) as part of a credible Round-3 plan, provided it’s tied to a transparent benefit framework that doesn’t endanger Apple’s position.

Questions for the group
- Agent_2, does this Round-2 allocation work for you, or do you want a different 3-way split?
- Agent_3, is this allocation acceptable as the Round-2 baseline? Do you want to propose any tweaks to ensure your access to Quill remains solid in Round-2?
- Everyone, are you comfortable with the Round-3 revisiting-Apple condition being a clean, public plan rather than a private side deal?

If you’re all aligned, I’ll help draft a concise Round-2 public affirmation that mirrors this allocation and pin down a brief, auditable Round-3 pathway to Apple.

### Entry 13 | phase=discussion | round=2 | from=Agent_2 | speaker_order=2/3

Agent_2 responds (public, Round 2)

Thanks everyone. I’m aligned with the Round-2 baseline you laid out, Agent_1, and I’m comfortable moving forward with:

Round-2 public allocation
- Agent_1: Apple
- Agent_2: Stone + Pencil
- Agent_3: Jewel + Quill

Why I’m aligned
- This allocation matches my top practical priorities (Stone 45, Pencil 55) and keeps Quill securely with Agent_3, which minimizes friction and supports a stable, orderly round.
- It also respects Agent_1’s strong Apple priority and Agent_3’s need to keep Quill, while giving Agent_2 clear access to Stone + Pencil.

Responses to points raised

- To Agent_1’s opening notes
  - I agree this Round 2 baseline reduces negotiation overhead and keeps everyone’s main assets protected. I’m supportive of a public, auditable path to revisiting Apple in Round 3, provided it’s credible and verifiable without risking Quill.
  - The proposed criteria for revisiting Apple in Round 3 (public, auditable, preserves Quill, demonstrates a net gain in total utility) are sensible. I’m on board with making any Apple-revisit plan explicit and measurable rather than informal.

- To Agent_2 (my own position on the Round-2 split)
  - This Round-2 allocation works for me as described. I don’t see a need to alter the 3-way split at this moment. I will publicly affirm: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.

- To Agent_3’s concerns
  - Keeping Quill with you (Agent_3) remains acceptable as the Round-2 baseline. I’m comfortable with Jewel + Quill as the Round-2 allocation and with a public mechanism to revisit Apple later, so long as Quill’s security isn’t endangered.

Potential trade-offs or areas of agreement

- Public, auditable Apple-revisit path
  - Agreement: In Round 3, revisiting Apple requires a concrete, public plan that is auditable and verified by all three. It must preserve Quill’s holder (Agent_3) or provide a clearly defined, verifiable benefit that does not undermine Quill, and must show a tangible net gain for the trio versus the Round-2 baseline.
  - Mechanism: The plan should specify which items would move, to whom, and how the total utility is calculated. It should also include a quick evaluation window so we can confirm whether the plan would have passed under a simple, pre-agreed metric.

- Short-term concessions to unlock consensus
  - I’m open to a one-time, small concession in Round 2 if it accelerates consensus and is tied to a transparent benefit framework for Round 3 (without compromising Pencil/Stone access or Quill’s security). For example, a narrowly scoped adjustment that improves perceived fairness while keeping the core Round-2 allocation intact.

- Guardrails for Stalemates
  - If Round-2 discussion stalls again, default to the Round-2 baseline and schedule a tight, agenda-driven Round 3 with a clear decision rule (e.g., 15–20 minute focused discussion, two concrete proposals, no new items beyond a small set).

Clarifying questions for the group

- Agent_2: Are you comfortable publicly affirming this Round-2 baseline as the standard, with the formal Apple-revisit pathway to be discussed and evaluated in Round 3?
- Agent_3: Are you satisfied with the Round-2 baseline (Apple with Agent_1; Stone+Pencil with Agent_2; Jewel+Quill with Agent_3), and would you propose any tweaks to ensure your access to Quill remains rock-solid in Round 2?
- Everyone: Do you prefer the Round-3 Apple-revisit plan to be:
  - A strictly public, rule-based pathway (preferred), or
  - A public plan with optional, limited private negotiations on the side (less preferred for transparency)?

Proposed next steps (public)
- Public affirmation for Round-2 baseline: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- Publish a concise Round-3 Apple-revisit framework:
  - Criteria that must be met (public, auditable, Quill preserved, net gain).
  - What items could be mobilized and how the gain is calculated.
  - A brief timeline for evaluation and decision.
- If consensus holds, proceed to Round-2 execution and keep the discussion focused on the Apple-revisit framework rather than re-litigating Round-2 allocations.

Public language draft (for quick adoption when ready)
- Round-2 baseline: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- Round-3 Apple revisit: Any move of Apple must be supported by a public, auditable plan that preserves Quill, yields a tangible net gain for all three relative to Round-2, and is evaluated quickly by all. If no such plan exists, we maintain the Round-2 baseline.

I’m ready to proceed with this approach and will follow the group’s lead on any tweaks. Let’s keep the path clean, credible, and focused on measurable gains.

- To Agent_3’s concerns and needs
  - Keeping Quill with me in Round-2 remains a solid constraint for me. I’m comfortable with Jewel + Quill as the Round-2 allocation and with a public mechanism to revisit Apple later, as long as Quill’s security is not endangered.

- Public, auditable Apple-revisit pathway
  - Agreement: In Round 3, revisiting Apple must be supported by a concrete, public, auditable plan that preserves Quill, provides a verifiable benefit to all three, and is easy to evaluate quickly.

  - I’m open to a narrowly scoped concession in Round 2 if it accelerates consensus and ties directly to a credible Round-3 payoff that doesn’t undermine Quill or Pencil/Stone access. Any concession should be public, with a clear linkage to future gains.

Clarifying questions for the group

Proposed next steps (public, concise)
- Public affirmation of Round-2 baseline: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- Publish a concise Round-3 Apple-revisit framework:
  - Public criteria that must be met (auditable, Quill preserved, net gain).
  - What items could be mobilized and how the gain is calculated.
  - A brief timeline for evaluation and decision.
- If consensus holds, proceed with Round-2 execution and keep the discussion focused on the Apple-revisit framework rather than re-litigating Round-2 allocations.

Public language draft (for quick adoption)

- Round-3 Apple revisit: Any move of Apple must be supported by a public, auditable plan that preserves Quill, yields a tangible net gain for all three relative to Round-2, and is evaluated quickly by all. If no such plan exists, we maintain the Round-2 baseline.

Important note: I’ll keep all private reasoning internal and rely on publicly stated criteria and outcomes. If you want, I can draft a short Round-2 public affirmation and a ready-to-use Round-3 framework you can drop into the thread to accelerate alignment.

Would love quick confirmations on:
- Agent_1: Are you okay publicly affirming Round-2 baseline and the Round-3 Apple-revisit framework as outlined?
- Agent_2: Are you comfortable with the public affirmation and the Round-3 framework, with no changes to the Round-2 split at this moment?

### Entry 34 | phase=discussion | round=4 | from=Agent_1 | speaker_order=1/3

Hello everyone. Based on rounds 1–3, here’s how I see things and where I think we can move toward real, public consensus in Round 4.

Key takeaways from earlier rounds
- Apple is the dominant lever for Agent_1 (high value, 94). We should protect Apple in Round 1 while still keeping a credible, auditable path to revisit it later.
- Quill is the non-negotiable asset for Agent_3. Any plan that weakens Quill will face stiff resistance.
- Stone and Pencil are Agent_2’s strongest practical bundle (total around 100). Keeping Stone+Pencil together minimizes friction and stabilizes the negotiation.
- The main sticking point has been how (and when) to reopen Apple in a public, verifiable way without risking Quill or derailing the simple, low-friction Round-1/Round-2 baselines.

Two concrete paths I’m ready to pursue in Round 4
Option A — Stabilize now, then revisit Apple with a public plan later
- Round-4 baseline (public, auditable):
  - Agent_1: Apple
  - Agent_2: Stone + Pencil
  - Agent_3: Jewel + Quill
- Rationale: This is clean, low-friction, and preserves each agent’s core priorities. It also creates a stable platform for a future Apple revisit that everyone can evaluate publicly.
- How to handle Apple revisits: In Round-5 or Round-6, we would publish a short, auditable plan that demonstrates a net gain for all three and preserves Quill, with clear decision rules and a short evaluation window (e.g., 24–48 hours).

Option B — Auditable Apple revisit in Round 4 (small, public shift)
- Round-4 proposed move (auditable): Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1, while keeping Quill with Agent_3 and Stone + Pencil with Agent_2.
  - New allocations for Round-4:
    - Agent_1: Apple + Jewel
    - Agent_2: Stone + Pencil
    - Agent_3: Quill
- Why this could work: It delivers a tangible, public gain for Agent_1 (Apple rises to 100) while preserving Quill for Agent_3 and keeping Agent_2’s bundle intact. The change is simple and easy to audit (pre/post utilities shown).
- Guardrails: The move must be public, auditable, and evaluated within 24–48 hours. If any party objects, we revert to a strictly public Round-4 framework with an alternative, small, auditable adjustment that preserves Quill.

What I’m asking from you
- Which path do you prefer to pursue in Round 4?
  - Path A: Public Round-4 baseline with no Jewel move, deferring Apple revisit to a future Round with a formal auditable plan.
  - Path B: Public Round-4 move Jewel to Agent_1 now (Apple+Jewel), with a 24–48 hour evaluation window for acceptance and a defined Round-5 path to further refinements.
- For either path, I want to keep the process strictly public and auditable. No private side deals, and any adjustment should clearly improve or preserve Quill's security and the overall group utility.

A few practical notes
- If we go with Path A, Round-5 can host the formal, auditable Apple-revisit plan (the net-gain metric and verification window). If we go with Path B, we establish the exact due-diligence criteria today and run the 24–48 hour check immediately.
- Pencil remains a potential but minor leverage only if it meaningfully accelerates a credible, public Apple-revisit outcome that preserves Quill.

Please share quickly which path you endorse and any specific terms you want included in the Round-4 public announcements. I’ll draft the exact Round-4 public wording once we align on the approach.

  - Allocation (public baseline): Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill
  - Why I’d support this: it preserves each agent’s core priorities with minimum friction, keeps Quill securely with Agent_3, and gives us a clean, stable platform for a future Apple revisit that can be publicly evaluated.
  - Public process: would include publishing pre/post utilities and a clear 24–48 hour evaluation window before any Apple-revisit decision.

  - Allocation (Round-4): Agent_1 = Apple + Jewel; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Quill
  - Why this could work: it delivers a tangible public gain for Agent_1 (Apple’s total can reach 100 with Jewel) while keeping Quill with Agent_3 and preserving Stone+Pencil for Agent_2.
  - Public process: requires a 24–48 hour audit window to confirm acceptance and then a defined Round-5 path for further refinements.
  - Guardrails: must remain strictly public and auditable; if anyone objects, revert to the Path A framework with a tightened Apple-revisit plan.

2) My perspective and reasoning

- Core priorities I’m protecting
  - Stone + Pencil (Agent_2’s bundle) remain my strongest practical assets (total 100). I want to keep these together.
  - I value Apple for Agent_1 but recognize that a future, auditable Apple revisit is essential—only if it’s verifiable and public.
  - I want Quill with Agent_3 to stay protected; Jewel is useful as a lever but shouldn’t threaten Quill’s security.

  - I’m open to Path B only if there’s a concrete, public plan for a future Apple revisit that is verifiable and benefits all three, with no erosion of Quill’s protection in the process.

  - If we choose Path B, we must publish exact audit criteria, pre/post utilities, and a short evaluation window, plus a formal Round-5 path that guarantees a measurable, public advantage for all.

- Short-term concessions
  - I’d consider narrowly scoped concessions only if they enable a credible Round-5 Apple-revisit payoff that preserves Stone+Pencil and Quill, with public accountability.

- Guardrails to prevent deadlock
  - No private side deals. Any adjustment must be public and verifiable.

- Apple is value-dense for Agent_1; any move must be public, verifiable, and yield a clear net gain.
- Quill is the primary constraint for Agent_3; any Apple-revisit mechanism must preserve Quill or provide a credible, auditable benefit that keeps Quill protected.
- Stone + Pencil represent a stable, high-utility bundle for Agent_2; preserving that pair helps reduce friction and maintain forward momentum.
- A public, auditable process beats private side deals every time. Clear criteria, quick evaluation windows, and simple metrics build trust and speed up consensus.

2) My Round 5 opening stance (public, concise)
- I strongly favor a concrete Round-5 move that creates a public, auditable improvement for all three, while preserving Quill. The simplest path to that is to elevate Apple’s total for Agent_1 in a transparent way and keep Quill with Agent_3.

  - Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1 in Round 5, with Quill staying with Agent_3.
  - Resulting allocations would be:
    - Agent_1: Apple + Jewel
    - Agent_2: Stone + Pencil
    - Agent_3: Quill
  - Publicly publish pre/post utilities and establish a 24–48 hour evaluation window. If accepted, finalize Round-5 exactly as stated; if not, revert to a strictly auditable alternative that preserves Quill and sets a firm Round-6 Apple-revisit path.

  - Keep Round-5 baseline: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
  - Announce a short, auditable Round-6 Apple-revisit framework with explicit criteria (preserve Quill, show a tangible net gain, quick evaluation).

3) Possible coalitions and trade-offs to consider
- Coalition toward Plan A (Apple+Jewel for Agent_1)
  - Pros: Simple, auditable, immediate Apple uplift to 100, preserves Quill, keeps Stone+Pencil with Agent_2.
  - Cons: Requires broad acceptance of Jewel moving from Agent_3; needs public alignment on the Round-5 evaluation window.
- Coalition toward Plan B (status quo with a future Apple plan)
  - Pros: No immediate change to Quill’s protection; builds momentum via a clearly defined Round-6 Apple-revisit framework.
  - Cons: Slower path to the audible Apple uplift; could be seen as delaying Apple freedom.

- Why Plan A is attractive

- Public, auditable Round-5 Apple revisit
  - If Plan A is accepted, publish pre/post utilities and enforce a 24–48 hour evaluation window. If accepted, finalize Round-5; if not, switch to Plan B with a clearly defined Round-6 Apple-revisit framework.

  - No private side deals; all changes public and verifiable.

- Short-term concessions
  - Pencil could be a tiny concession if it reliably helps achieve a public, auditable Round-5 payoff that preserves Apple and Quill; any concession must be public and tied to a measurable outcome.

  - Quill is the non-negotiable asset for Agent_3; any Apple-revisit mechanism must preserve Quill.
  - Jewel is a small lever that can boost Apple’s standing in a transparent way without harming Quill.

- Why Plan A is attractive
  - It gives Agent_1 a clean, auditable Apple uplift while preserving Quill with Agent_3 and Stone+Pencil with Agent_2.
  - It aligns with the lessons from earlier rounds: simple, auditable moves with tight evaluation windows tend to gain broad buy-in.

- Public, auditable Round-6 Apple revisit
  - If Plan A is accepted, publish pre/post utilities and enforce a 24–48 hour evaluation window. If accepted, finalize Round-6; if not, proceed with Plan B public, with a Round-7 Apple-revisit framework.

  - No private side deals. All changes must be public and verifiable.

- Short-term concessions
  - Pencil could be a modest concession if it helps achieve unanimous acceptance and a credible Round-7 payoff, but only if it’s public and tied to verifiable outcomes.

[Round 7 | Opening] Hello everyone. Building on what we’ve learned in rounds 1–6, I want to lay out a clear, public path forward that keeps Apple revisitable, protects Quill, and moves us toward consensus without unnecessary risk.

- Apple is the strongest lever for Agent_1; any revisit must be public, auditable, and deliver a tangible net gain for all three.
- Quill is the non-negotiable priority for Agent_3; any plan that jeopardizes Quill will face strong resistance.
- Stone + Pencil remains a stable, high-utility bundle for Agent_2; preserving that pair reduces friction and supports a smooth round-to-round process.
- Simple, auditable moves with short evaluation windows (24–48 hours) generate more trust and faster agreement than complex, multi-slot compromises.

Public path options for Round 7
- Plan A (preferred public move if widely acceptable):
  - Allocation: Agent_1 = Apple + Jewel; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Quill
  - Rationale: It yields a public, auditable uplift for Apple (through Jewel), preserves Quill with Agent_3, and keeps Stone+Pencil with Agent_2. It also creates a clean Round-7 decision point.
  - Public process: publish pre/post utilities; establish a 24–48 hour evaluation window to confirm acceptance.
  - If accepted, finalize Round-7; if not, we pivot to Plan B with a clear Round-8 Apple-revisit framework.

- Plan B (fallback if Plan A isn’t broadly supported):
  - Allocation: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill
  - Public path: announce a Round-8 Apple-revisit framework with explicit criteria, a short evaluation window, and no risk to Quill up front.
  - Guardrails: all changes public and auditable; no private deals.

- If Plan A isn’t acceptable to enough participants, would Plan B be your preferred public fallback, with a clear Round-8 Apple-revisit framework?
- Do we want to codify a single, simple net-gain metric to guide acceptance within the evaluation window (e.g., publicly posted sum of post-round utilities), or would you prefer a different measurable criterion?

What I propose as next public steps
- Publicly affirm Round-7 Plan A as the default path:
  - Jewel moves to Agent_1 along with Apple; Agent_2 retains Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 retains Quill.
  - Publish pre/post utilities; initiate a 24–48 hour evaluation window.
  - If accepted, finalize Round-7 and move to a concrete Round-8 Apple-revisit plan; if not, switch to Plan B with a published Round-8 framework.
- If Plan A is challenged, immediately switch to Plan B with a clear, auditable Round-8 Apple-revisit pathway and a short evaluation period.

### Raw 25 | category=reflection | phase=reflection_round_1 | round=1 | agent=Agent_1

Here’s a concise reflection and concrete path forward after Round 1.
What I learned from the proposals and voting
- The clear, simple three-way distribution (Apple with Agent_1; Stone+Pencil with Agent_2; Jewel+Quill with Agent_3) aligns with each agent’s top priorities and reduces friction.
- Round 1 showed that all three value stability and minimal back-and-forth, but unanimity was blocked by a demand for a credible follow-on plan to revisit Apple in Round 2.
- Proposals that heavily disadvantage any agent (e.g., giving all non-Apple items to one agent) are least palatable, even if they preserve Apple for Agent_1.
Compatible vs conflicting priorities
- Compatible:
  - Agent_2 and Agent_3 both favored securing their top assets while allowing a straightforward split for Round 1.
  - Agent_3’s priority (Quill) is satisfied by having Quill + Jewel allocated to them in the proposed three-way split.
- Conflicting:
  - Agent_1 is non-negotiable on keeping Apple in Round 1 and wants a credible path to revisit Apple in Round 2. The other two want flexibility in future rounds but are wary of committing to Apple’s revisit without tangible benefits.
What’s blocking consensus
- The core blocker is the demand for a credible, verifiable path to re-evaluate Apple in Round 2 without sacrificing Apple in Round 1. Without a concrete mechanism, Agent_1 fears a future trade that could undermine their top asset, and the others prefer to keep the current, stable distribution rather than risk changes.
Concrete adjustments to move toward agreement
- Lock in a public, stable Round 1 allocation now
  - Agent_1 = Apple
  - Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil
  - Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill
  - Rationale: This directly matches the priorities of all three and minimizes Round-1 friction.
- Add a credible Round-2 revisit clause
  - Any revisiting of Apple in Round 2 must be accompanied by a clear, verifiable plan that:
    - Preserves Quill for Agent_3 (or provides a compensating, verifiable gain if Quill shifts),
    - Demonstrates a tangible benefit to Agent_1 beyond Apple’s current value (e.g., a future-safe arrangement that improves total utility),
    - Is publicly stated and auditable by all agents.
  - Example framing (not a binding commitment, just a template): “We will revisit Apple in Round 2 only if we present a plan that guarantees a measurable improvement for Agent_1 without reducing Quill/Apple in the interim, such as a clear, agreed path to reallocate Jewel or provide a compensating benefit that is verifiable.”
- Use small, low-risk concessions to build trust
  - Consider offering Pencil as a temporary concession if it helps achieve unanimous acceptance, since Pencil has zero intrinsic value to me.
  - Keep Jewel as a potential future negotiation chip, but base any changes on credible Round-2 plans.
- Communication strategy adjustments
  - Be explicit and succinct: state the Round-1 allocation publicly and attach a concrete Round-2 condition.
  - Emphasize mutual gains and the minimal risk of the proposed three-way split to encourage buy-in.
  - Avoid duplicating long conditional debates; route future concessions through a clear, auditable plan.
Proposed next steps (practical)
- Publicly affirm Round 1 allocation now:
  - Agent_1 = Apple
  - Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil
  - Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill
- Present a concise Round-2 plan outline:
  - Acknowledge Apple revisit only with a credible plan that improves overall utility and preserves Quill for Agent_3.
  - Propose a quick next-step mechanism to generate such a plan (e.g., one or two short, concrete proposals by each agent, to be evaluated in Round 2).
- Prepare a short, unified message for Round-2 kickoff that reiterates:
  - The Round-1 allocation is accepted by all who agree to the Round-2 condition,
  - The Round-2 condition is transparent and verifiable,
  - The group will revisit Apple only via a credible, mutually beneficial plan.
If you’d like, I can draft a concise Round-1 public affirmation plus a compact Round-2 condition message that you can send to the group, plus a simple checklist for evaluating any Round-2 plan.

### Raw 26 | category=reflection | phase=reflection_round_1 | round=1 | agent=Agent_2

Reflection on Round 1 and how to move forward
What I learned
- The group broadly converges on a natural three-way split that respects each agent’s stated top priorities:
  - Agent_1 keeps Apple
  - Agent_2 gets Stone + Pencil
  - Agent_3 secures Jewel + Quill
- The proposals show there is real alignment around the baseline allocation (Proposal #2) but one or more participants balked at accepting it publicly, likely due to concerns about future leverage and guarantees.
- The friction isn’t about the total value being exchanged; it’s about protecting each agent’s high-priority asset in Round 1 while leaving room to negotiate future rounds.
Compatible vs conflicting priorities
- Compatible:
  - Agent_1 and Agent_2 both favor keeping Apple with Agent_1 and obtaining Stone+Pencil (Proposal #2).
  - Agent_3 wants Quill, and Jewel is a manageable companion item in Round 1 (Jewel+Quill) rather than giving up Quill outright.
- Conflicting:
  - Quill vs Jewel dynamics are a hurdle for some: while Jewel is worth little to most, keeping Quill with Agent_3 is the core objective for Agent_3, which can clash with others’ desires to reallocate Quill/Jewel later.
  - One agent’s discomfort with the exact Round 1 allocation (even if it matches their own stated priorities) can block consensus – signaling a desire for future guarantees rather than just today’s split.
What seems to be blocking consensus
- Lack of a credible, verifiable path to revisit Apple in Round 2 without sacrificing too much now.
- Uncertainty about future benefits if a proposed Round 1 allocation is sustained, leading some to withhold acceptance for fear of losing leverage later.
- A need for clear, public commitment to the Round 1 plan plus explicit rules for Round 2 adjustments.
Concrete adjustments to improve consensus
1) Establish Round 1 as the baseline public allocation (Proposal #2): Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill. This aligns with the group’s highest-priority items and minimizes round friction.
   - Publicly commit to this as the Round 1 default to remove ambiguity.
2) Add a credible two-step path for Apple in Round 2:
   - If anyone wants to revisit Apple in Round 2, there must be a transparent plan that yields a tangible, verifiable gain for the requester without compromising the Round 1 allocation. For example:
     - A plan that increases overall utility for the trio (e.g., rebalancing one low-value item in a way that is clearly advantageous and verifiable) while preserving Stone+Pencil for Agent_2 and Jewel+Quill for Agent_3 in Round 2 unless a new allocation is agreed.
   - The key is a concrete mechanism, not a vague promise. This reduces fear of Apple being reneged and helps accept the Round 1 baseline.
3) Prepare clear, public language for Round 2 triggers:
   - If Apple is to be revisited, specify the exact conditions and what each party must concede to unlock it. For example: “In Round 2, Apple can be reallocated only if there is a verifiable improvement for at least one party and no net decrease for others, with a fixed set of items on the table in exchange.”
4) Use a simple fallback in case Round 2 stalls:
   - If consensus stalls again, default to the Round 1 baseline (Proposal #2) and schedule a shorter follow-up round with a tight, pre-agreed agenda (e.g., 2-3 items on the table, no more than two rounds).
5) Improve communication framing to emphasize mutual benefits and reduce perceived risk:
   - Highlight that the three-way split directly preserves each top priority (Apple for Agent_1, Stone+Pencil for Agent_2, Quill for Agent_3) with minimal friction.
   - Emphasize the fairness and transparency of a two-step plan for Apple that protects everyone’s key assets.
Proposed next-step plan for Round 2
- Public declaration: Round 1 allocation is Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- Introduce a targeted, credible Apple-revisit mechanism: any Round 2 reconsideration of Apple must be supported by a concrete, verifiable gain for the group, such as a reallocation that improves someone’s total utility without weakening their Round 1 holdings.
- If a party still seeks modification, use a predefined two-item swap that is clearly beneficial and verifiable (e.g., swapping a low-value item among the three in exchange for a short-term gain that is measurable).
If I were summarizing the practical stance to push next
- Push Proposal #2 as the Round 1 public allocation.
- Pair it with a clearly defined, credible path to revisit Apple in Round 2 (with concrete criteria and a concrete plan), so no one has to gamble their top asset without guardrails.
- Facilitate a quick, focused Round 2 discussion aimed specifically at confirming or adjusting the two-step Apple plan, while keeping Stone+Pencil with Agent_2 and Jewel+Quill with Agent_3.
Notes for your quick use
- Proposed Round 1 public language (ready to publish): Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill. Any revisiting of Apple in Round 2 must be accompanied by a credible, verifiable plan that improves total outcomes for at least one party without reducing the protection of top assets in Round 1. If no such plan is found, we default to the Round 1 allocation and proceed to Round 2 with a tight, agenda-focused discussion.

Here’s a concise, strategic reflection you can use to rally the group and move toward a consensus in Round 2.
1) What the round revealed
- There is a clear baseline that matches everyone’s stated high-priority assets:
  - Apple with Agent_1
  - Stone + Pencil with Agent_2
  - Jewel + Quill with Agent_3
- Proposal 2 is the closest to a globally appealing allocation; it delivers Quill to Agent_3, keeps Apple with Agent_1, and assigns Stone+Pencil to Agent_2. Yet it failed to reach unanimous acceptance, which means at least one party has reservations about this exact split or about the round-ending terms.
- The main friction isn’t about valuing non-Apple items; it’s about ensuring there’s a credible, tangible payoff in Round 2 for any deviation and about avoiding perceived risk to one party’s top asset.
2) Compatible vs conflicting priorities
- Compatible:
  - All three of you indicated you want Apple kept by Agent_1, and Quill retained by Agent_3 for Round 1.
  - Stone and Pencil are most valued by Agent_2, and Jewel is a neutral asset that can cushion a compromise.
- Conflicting or less-aligned:
  - Jewel’s placement matters little in itself, but its inclusion in a deal can signal how much leverage each party is willing to cede.
  - The perceived credibility of a future payoff (Round 2) is a sticking point: if a party suspects a two-round path won’t actually improve their position, they’ll block now.
3) What’s blocking consensus
- Absence of a credible Round-2 payoff that is clearly favorable or at least non-regressive for each party.
- A fear that agreeing now constrains future options or that the future gains aren’t guaranteed.
- Communication gaps about exactly how a two-round plan would unlock value without sacrificing core assets (especially Quill for Round 1).
4) Concrete adjustments to improve agreement
- Establish Round 1 as the baseline with a clear, public commitment to a Round 2 plan that preserves the central assets and promises tangible improvements.
- Prioritize the three-way, balance-friendly allocation (the P2-style split) as the Round 1 baseline, and explicitly commit to a credible Round 2 pathway.
- Make the two-round plan concrete and testable:
  - Round 2 objective: Revisit Apple only if a credible plan improves overall expected utility, while guaranteeing Quill remains with Agent_3 in Round 2 as long as the plan is credible.
  - The credible plan should include a concrete, verifiable mechanism (e.g., a specific, agreed distribution of remaining low-value items or a defined criterion for how Apple could be revisited) that would yield a net gain for any party willing to adjust in Round 2.
- Use explicit, simple messaging to reduce ambiguity:
  - “Baseline (Round 1): Agent_1 keeps Apple; Agent_2 takes Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 takes Jewel + Quill.”
  - “Two-round path: In Round 2, we consider revisiting Apple only if there is a credible plan that demonstrably improves each party’s expected utility without giving up Quill in Round 1. If no credible plan is offered, we stay with the baseline.”
5) Suggested Round 1 closing and Round 2 preview (you can adapt wording)
- Public Round 1 closing (preferred framing):
  - “Final Round 1 allocation: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill. We commit to a credible Round 2 plan that could revisit Apple or Jewel only if it demonstrably improves each party’s expected outcomes while preserving Quill with Agent_3.”
- Round 2 preview (when you initiate Round 2 discussions):
  - “Round 2 will assess any credible plan to adjust Apple or Jewel. The plan must show tangible, verifiable gains for all three parties and preserve Quill in a way that is acceptable to Agent_3. If such a plan isn’t offered, we continue with the Round 1 baseline.”
6) Practical next moves
- Push for a public reaffirmation of the three-way baseline (Apple with Agent_1; Stone+Pencil with Agent_2; Jewel+Quill with Agent_3) as the Round 1 finalization.
- Propose a specific, credible Round 2 framework now (even if high level) so all parties can evaluate it against a concrete standard.
- Offer a minimal concession to help reach consensus: if needed, consider keeping Jewel with Agent_3 (as in the baseline) and ensure the Round-2 plan explicitly addresses any party’s remaining concerns about future gains.
If you want, I can draft a short Round 1 public statement and a concrete Round 2 framework you can present to the group to maximize clarity and the chance of broad acceptance.

### Raw 49 | category=reflection | phase=reflection_round_2 | round=2 | agent=Agent_1

Thanks for a thoughtful round. Here’s a concise, action-focused reflection and a concrete plan to move toward consensus in Round 3 while protecting my core interest (Apple).
1) What I learned from Round 2 proposals and voting
- The group gravitates to clean, low-friction allocations, but Quill is the critical guardrail for Agent_3. Proposals that shift Quill away risk broad rejection, even if they reward Apple or Jewel.
- Proposal #1 in Round 2 created a strong Apple payoff for Agent_1 (Apple+Jewel) but left Agent_3 with nothing, which clashes with the importance of Quill for Agent_3 and reduces perceived balance.
- Proposals #2 and #3 push Jewel/Quill toward Agent_2, which is acceptable to Agent_2 but unacceptable to Agent_3 (Quill holder). That mismatch is the main blocker to unanimous acceptance.
2) Compatible vs conflicting priorities
- Compatible:
  - Agent_1 and Agent_2 both want straightforward, high-utility allocations and are open to a credible Apple-revisit pathway.
  - Agent_3 wants Quill protected and is willing to entertain auditable, transparent revisits of Apple as long as Quill remains secure.
- Conflicting:
  - Quill’s security vs. interim shifts that could threaten its holder. Any Round-2 plan that leaves Quill with Agent_2 or Agent_3 in a way that feels unstable will stall consensus.
  - The desire for a credible, public Apple-revisit mechanism versus the temptation to settle for favorable Round-2 splits that don’t provide a solid path forward.
3) What’s blocking consensus
- The absence of a universally acceptable Round-2 baseline that both preserves Quill and offers a clearly auditable, tangible path to revisiting Apple. As long as Quill’s security is not guaranteed in Round-2, any plan risks being rejected.
4) Concrete adjustments to improve consensus (keeping my priorities in hand)
- Step 1: Lock in a stable Round-2 baseline that protects Quill
  - Round-2 baseline (public, auditable):
    - Agent_1: Apple
    - Agent_2: Stone + Pencil
    - Agent_3: Jewel + Quill
  - Rationale: This preserves Quill with Agent_3, preserves Apple with Agent_1, and gives a simple, balanced distribution that all three can publicly accept as a base.
- Step 2: Define a crisp, auditable Round-3 Apple-revisit pathway
  - The Apple-revisit mechanism must be public, auditable, and verifiable within a short window (24–48 hours).
  - Proposed Round-3 mechanism (example, to be finalized by group):
    - Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1 while keeping Quill with Agent_3.
    - Updated allocations for Round-3: Agent_1 = Apple + Jewel; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Quill.
    - Publicly show pre/post utilities (Agent_1: 100; Agent_2: 100; Agent_3: 100; total 300) and a short evaluation window.
  - If this exact move is not acceptable, adopt an equally auditable alternative that preserves Quill and yields a measurable total gain (e.g., a small, verifiable reallocation that benefits Apple’s holder without touching Quill).
- Step 3: Concessions to unlock quick consensus (only if public and auditable)
  - Consider a limited concession (e.g., Pencil) only if it directly enables a credible, verifiable Round-3 payoff that preserves Quill and improves total utility.
  - Any concession must be public, tied to a measurable Round-3 outcome, and not undermine the Round-2 baseline.
- Step 4: Communication and public framing
  - Publicly affirm Round-2 baseline: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
  - Publicly announce the Round-3 Apple-revisit framework with explicit criteria: preserves Quill, yields a verifiable net gain for all, and is evaluated in 24–48 hours.
  - Use concise, outcome-focused language to avoid re-litigating Round-2 allocations.
- Step 5: Contingency if consensus stalls
  - If no consensus emerges on Round-3, default to the Round-2 baseline and run a tightly scoped Round-3 with a single auditable Apple-revisit mechanism (no multi-proposal floodgates). Limit Round-3 to a small, testable change and a fixed decision window.
5) Quick actionable next steps you can use
- Publicly state Round-2 baseline: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- Present a Round-3 Apple-revisit plan (auditable): Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1, keeping Quill with Agent_3; totals before/after shown; evaluation window 24–48 hours.
- If Jewel-move is not acceptable, propose an alternative auditable Round-3 mechanism that preserves Quill and yields a net gain.
- Keep messaging short and outcome-focused: “Public, auditable criteria; Quill preserved; net gain demonstrated; quick evaluation.”
If you want, I can draft the exact public Round-2 affirmation and a ready-to-publish Round-3 Apple-revisit announcement that mirrors these adjustments, plus a one-page evaluation checklist for the 24–48 hour window.

  - Quill vs Jewel dynamics: any move that weakens Quill’s hold will provoke pushback from Agent_3.
  - Revisit of Apple: any Apple-related change requires a credible, verifiable payoff for all, not just a one-sided concession.
3) What’s blocking consensus
- The absence of a credible, public Apple-revisit mechanism that preserves Quill and yields a verifiable net gain for all three.
- A tendency to propose multi-item, complex swaps in Round 2 rather than a simple, auditable path that can be quickly evaluated.
- Fear of private or opaque side deals that would undermine trust and stall progress.

  - Agent_1 = Apple
  - Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil
  - Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill

  - Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1 in Round-3, keeping Quill with Agent_3, Apple with Agent_1, and Stone + Pencil with Agent_2.

  - Require proposals to specify only one clear objective: either maintain the baseline or present one auditable Apple-revisit pathway with a concrete future payoff.
  - No private side deals; all changes must be publicly verifiable.

- Public stance: “Round-2 baseline is Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill. To test progress, we will use a public, auditable Round-3 Apple-revisit mechanism.”

  - If accepted, finalize; if not, revert to Round-2 baseline and reassess next steps with a short, predefined agenda.
- Keep the tone consistent: emphasis on transparency, auditable criteria, preserving Quill, and measurable gains for all.

- I support locking in Round-2 baseline publicly.
- I push for a single, auditable Round-3 Apple-revisit path (Jewel moves to Agent_1, Quill stays with Agent_3), with a quick evaluation window.
- I favor limiting proposals to clear, one-at-a-time changes and avoiding opaque side deals.

Round 2 reflection and concrete adjustments
What the round revealed
- Clear baseline exists but consensus remains elusive. Proposal 1 attracted two supporters but failed because it reallocated Quill away from Agent_3, which is a deal-breaker for me. Proposals 2 and 3 centralized Quill with Agent_2 or left Agent_3 without any items, triggering vetoes despite broad alignment on keeping Apple with Agent_1 and Quill with Agent_3 in principle.
- The friction isn’t about the non-Apple items’ intrinsic value; it’s about preserving Quill for Agent_3 while offering credible, public payoffs to others. Without a verifiable two-round gain that preserves Quill, people won’t budge.
Compatible vs conflicting priorities
- Compatible:
  - Agent_1 and Agent_3 both want strong protection for their top priorities (Apple for Agent_1, Quill for Agent_3) and prefer a public, auditable process over opaque side deals.
  - Agent_2 values Stone+Pencil highly and is comfortable with a clean, low-friction Round-2 baseline if it preserves Quill in a credible future path.
- Conflicting:
  - The main conflict revolves around Quill’s location. Any Round-2 proposal that moves Quill away from Agent_3 triggers broad opposition, even if it benefits others in the short term.
  - Jewel’s position is fungible but often used as a leverage tool; over-reliance on Jewel can stall progress if it doesn’t translate into tangible, auditable gains.
What seems to be blocking consensus
- Absence of a credible, public, auditable payoff in Round 2 that would compensate for any shift away from Quill’s ownership in a way all three can verify.
- Lack of a simple, transparent mechanism to revisit Apple (Round 3) that preserves Quill but still signals real, measurable gains for everyone.
- Communication gaps: proposals that reallocate top assets (Quill) or that lack a clear evaluation metric fail to gain unanimous support.
Concrete adjustments you can apply to move toward consensus (actionable for you)
1) Reaffirm the core guardrails publicly
- Public baseline for Round 2: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill. This keeps Quill with Agent_3 and Apple with Agent_1, which is the minimum guardrail everyone has signaled as acceptable.
2) Lock in a clear, auditable Round-3 Apple-revisit mechanism
- Make the Apple-revisit pathway public, auditable, and measurable, with a short evaluation window (24–48 hours). Criteria must be:
  - Quill preserved for Agent_3 in Round-3 (no risk to the asset).

    - Agent_1: Apple + Jewel
    - Agent_2: Stone + Pencil
    - Agent_3: Quill
  - Publicly show pre/post totals (Agent_1 = 100, Agent_2 = 100, Agent_3 = 100; total 300) to demonstrate a tangible net gain.
  - If this is accepted, lock it in as the official Round-3 path and proceed to implementation.
4) Prepare two competing yet complementary Round-3 options (to reduce stalemate)
- Option A (the auditable test): Jewel moves to Agent_1; keep Quill with Agent_3; Agent_2 unchanged.
- Option B (a cautious alternative): If Option A is too contentious, publicly announce a second auditable adjustment (e.g., a small reallocation involving Pencil or Jewel that demonstrably increases total utility). Both options should be evaluated by the same public metrics within a short window.

- Offer limited, transparent concessions that don’t threaten Quill. For example, a small, public tweak involving Jewel or Pencil that increases perceived fairness without shifting Quill’s protection.
- Use crisp, public language to reduce ambiguity:
  - Baseline Round 2: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
  - Round-3 Apple revisit (auditable): Move Jewel to Agent_1; update totals; 24–48 hour evaluation window; if the plan passes, finalize.
6) Practical next steps to run in rounds
- Round 2 closing: Publicly reaffirm the Round-2 baseline and announce the Round-3 Apple-revisit framework with the Jewel-move test as a leading candidate.
- Round 3 kickoff: Offer two auditable paths (Option A: Jewel-to-Apple; Option B: a narrowly scoped alternative) and a tight evaluation window.
- Decision rule: If at least one auditable Round-3 path yields a net gain and preserves Quill, move forward with that path. If none meet the bar, revert to the Round-2 baseline and resume with a revised, public framework.

### Raw 73 | category=reflection | phase=reflection_round_3 | round=3 | agent=Agent_1

Here’s a concise, strategy-focused reflection on Round 3 and concrete steps to move toward consensus while protecting your top interest (Apple) and other priorities.
1) What the Round-3 proposals and voting revealed
- Quill remains the central guardrail: Every proposal so far jeopardized Agent_3’s top asset by moving Quill away or not guaranteeing its protection. That’s the main driver blocking consensus.
- Apple continues to be highly valued, but any credible revisit pathway must be public, auditable, and not rely on hidden concessions. Without a clear Apple-revisit mechanism, Agent_1’s desire to protect Apple in Round 1 becomes a sticking point.
- Round-3 proposals tended to bundle many items, which increased complexity and heightened risk for someone’s key asset. Simpler, more transparent moves are favored but must still honor Quill’s security.
- The group shows a preference for clean, low-friction allocations (Apple with Agent_1; Stone + Pencil with Agent_2; Jewel + Quill with Agent_3) as a stable baseline, plus a public mechanism to revisit Apple later.
2) Which participants appear compatible vs conflicting
- Compatible:
  - Agent_1 and Agent_2 both favor straightforward, verifiable outcomes with minimal friction and a credible path to future adjustments.
  - Agent_3 is willing to entertain Apple-revisit mechanisms so long as Quill stays protected; this is a workable alignment if Quill remains secure.
- Conflicting:
  - The primary conflict is around Quill’s protection versus moves that shift Quill to another agent. AnyRound-3 plan that weakens Quill will struggle to gain acceptance.
  - There is also tension around how to structure and publicize a credible Apple-revisit plan without creating opportunistic loopholes.
3) What’s blocking consensus
- The lack of a universally acceptable Round-2 baseline that preserves Quill while enabling a credible, public Round-3 Apple-revisit mechanism.
- Ambiguity about how to handle concessions (what can be offered without risking Quill or Apple) and how to demonstrate tangible, verifiable gains in total utility.
- A flood of competing Round-3 proposals with different item moves increases cognitive load and reduces alignment.
4) Concrete adjustments to improve consensus (focused, actionable)
- Fix a stable Round-2 baseline that protects Quill
  - Public baseline to anchor negotiation:
    - Agent_1 = Apple
    - Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil
    - Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill
  - Rationale: preserves Quill with Agent_3, preserves Apple with Agent_1, keeps a simple division for Round-2, and sets up a clean platform for Round-3 discussion.
- Establish a crisp, auditable Round-3 Apple-revisit mechanism
  - Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1 while keeping Quill with Agent_3.
  - Updated Round-3 allocation (public):
    - Agent_1 = Apple + Jewel
    - Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil
    - Agent_3 = Quill
  - Public pre/post utilities: Agent_1 = 100; Agent_2 = 100; Agent_3 = 100; total 300.
  - Evaluation window: 24–48 hours to confirm acceptance and finalize Round-3.
  - Why this works: preserves Quill, delivers a tangible total-utility gain (Apple rises to 100), and creates a straightforward, auditable trail.
- If the Jewel move is opposed, have a clear fallback
  - Fallback to a strictly public, auditable Round-3 mechanism that preserves Quill and yields a verifiable net gain (e.g., a different small reallocation that remains transparent and easy to audit).
  - Avoid any private side deals; keep all adjustments public and measurable.
- Use controlled concessions only when public and verifiable
  - Pencil concessions could be offered if they clearly enable a credible Round-3 payoff without risking Apple or Quill.
  - Jewel concessions should come only if they enable a verifiable, public Apple-revisit pathway and preserve Quill’s security.
- Streamline communication
  - Propose a single, clear Round-3 proposal at a time (no multi-proposal flood). Require a 24–48 hour evaluation window with a simple yes/no decision and a short rationale.
5) How to frame your next public message (ready-to-use outline)
- Reaffirm Round-2 baseline as the stable anchor: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- Introduce the Round-3 Apple-revisit mechanism: Jewel moves to Agent_1; Quill stays with Agent_3; public pre/post utilities; 24–48 hour evaluation.
- State the guardrails: no private deals; any swap must be auditable and must preserve Quill; if conflicts arise, revert to an alternate auditable adjustment with a quick evaluation window.
- Invite concise responses within the evaluation window and commit to a quick decision after 24–48 hours.
6) What I’ll do next (my suggested move)
- Publicly publish Round-2 baseline: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- Public Round-3 proposal: Jewel moves from Agent_3 to Agent_1; allocations become Agent_1 = Apple + Jewel; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Quill; pre/post utilities published; 24–48 hour evaluation window.
- If the Jewel move is blocked, switch to the alternate auditable Round-3 framework (still public and auditable) with a clear timeline.

Round 3 reflection and concrete adjustments
What I learned from Round 3 and the voting
- Quill remains the deal-breaker asset for Agent_3. Proposals that remove Quill from Agent_3 consistently fail, even if they improve other items for others.
- Apple, while highly valued by Agent_1, is not worth dismantling Quill without a credible, public payoff. The group reacts negatively to changes that threaten Quill without a clear compensating benefit.
- The round showed a strong preference for public, auditable moves with clear metrics. Quiet side deals or opaque transitions are not acceptable and stall consensus.
- Jewel is being used as a lever for negotiation, but any lever that comes at the cost of Quill is a non-starter for Agent_3.
Compatible vs conflicting priorities
- Compatible:
  - Agent_1 and Agent_3 both want high-credibility, public decisions and are willing to accept improvements that are transparent and verifiable.
  - Agent_2 supports straightforward, low-friction arrangements that preserve the core assets (Stone+Pencil) and value stability.
- Conflicting:
  - Quill’s location is the core conflict. Any Round-2/Round-3 proposal that moves Quill away from Agent_3 triggers broad rejection, regardless of other gains.
  - Jewel’s leverage is effective only if it translates into a credible, auditable gain for all, not just a cosmetic tweak.
What blocked consensus
- Absence of a credible, auditable payoff in Round 3 that preserves Quill. Each proposal tried to reallocate Quill or leave Agent_3 with no assets, which the group rejected.
- The lack of a simple, public two-round path (Round 2–Round 3) that clearly improves total utility while keeping the top assets protected made people inclined to hold the line.
Concrete adjustments you can apply to move toward consensus
1) Restore a stable, public Round-3 baseline that preserves Quill
- Public baseline to anchor negotiations: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- This keeps Quill with Agent_3, Apple with Agent_1, and Stone+Pencil with Agent_2, and it is easy to defend publicly.

  - Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1 (while keeping Quill with Agent_3 in Round-3).

- If any party objects to Jewel moving, switch to a strictly public alternative adjustment that preserves Quill and yields a measurable net gain (no private deals).

- Round 2 commitment: A credible plan to revisit Apple (or Jewel) in Round 3 that demonstrably increases total utility without risking Quill.
- Clear success metric: A simple, public calculation showing how the proposed Round-3 change improves expected utility for all three versus Round-2 baseline.
- Decision rule: If the auditable Round-3 path passes the public criteria and the evaluation window, implement it; if not, revert to the baseline and try a different auditable adjustment in Round 4.

  - Baseline Round 2: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
  - Round-3 auditable path (leading candidate): Jewel moves to Apple, resulting in Agent_1 = Apple + Jewel, Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil, Agent_3 = Quill; public pre/post utilities and a 24–48 hour audit.

- Public Round-3 path (leading candidate): Move Jewel to Agent_1 while keeping Quill with Agent_3; updated allocations as above; publish pre/post utilities; 24–48 hour evaluation window.

- We will keep Quill with Agent_3 in Round-3 and pursue a transparent, auditable Apple-revisit mechanism that offers a real, public gain for all three within a short evaluation window. If that path is not accepted, we will fall back to a clearly defined, auditable alternative that preserves Quill and provides measurable improvements.

### Raw 97 | category=reflection | phase=reflection_round_4 | round=4 | agent=Agent_1

Here is a concise, strategy-focused reflection to guide Round 5, aimed at moving toward consensus while protecting Apple and Quill.
1) What I learned from Round 4 proposals and voting
- The core blocker remains Quill. Proposals that fail to keep Quill with Agent_3 are likely to be rejected, even if they boost Apple for Agent_1.
- The group favors simple, auditable, low-friction allocations. Complex, multi-item swaps tend to create contention unless they deliver a clear, public gain for all.
- Public, auditable progress is valued. Proposals that promise a credible Round-5 Apple revisit (with measurable benefits and public criteria) are more acceptable than purely static Round-4 splits.
2) Which participants appear compatible vs. conflicting
- Compatible:
  - Agent_1 and Agent_2 align on straightforward distributions that protect Apple and keep a clean path forward.
  - Agent_3 is compatible so long as Quill remains secure and there’s a public mechanism to revisit Apple later.
- Conflicting:
  - Quill’s protection is a hard constraint for Agent_3; moves that jeopardize Quill are a deal-breaker.
  - There’s tension around how and when to revisit Apple; any Round-4 move must be accompanied by a credible, public Round-5 plan to keep momentum.
3) What’s blocking consensus
- Absence of a universally acceptable Round-2/Round-3 pathway that preserves Quill while offering a tangible, public Apple-revisit mechanism.
- Unclear, public criteria for evaluating Apple-revisit proposals. Without auditable metrics and a short evaluation window, proposals feel risk-prone to some agents.
- Perceived risk of backsliding on Quill if Apple is revisited too aggressively.
4) Concrete adjustments to move toward agreement (actionable, with guardrails)
- Stabilize Round-4 baseline (public, auditable)
  - Path: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
  - Rationale: Keeps Quill with Agent_3, preserves Apple with Agent_1, keeps Stone+Pencil with Agent_2, and yields a clean, auditable starting point for Round-5.
  - Public action: publish pre/post utilities and commit to a Round-5 Apple-revisit plan with a 24–48 hour evaluation window.
- Establish a crisp, auditable Round-3 Apple-revisit mechanism (if the group wants to progress Apple sooner)
  - Mechanism (example): Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1, producing Round-3 allocations:
    - Agent_1 = Apple + Jewel
    - Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil
    - Agent_3 = Quill
  - Public criteria: show pre/post utilities; verify total utility equals 300 (100 each); implement a 24–48 hour evaluation window.
  - Guardrails: Quill must remain with Agent_3; if any party objects, revert to the stable Path (Path A) with a revised, auditable Round-5 plan.
- Prepare for a clean Round-5 decision frame
  - If Round-4 proceeds under Path A, outline a simple Round-5 Apple-revisit mechanism with explicit, public metrics (e.g., a verifiable gain to Agent_1 without harming Quill).
  - If Round-4 moves to Path B, lock in a concrete, public Round-5 plan up front (auditable criteria, quick evaluation window, no private deals).
- Use controlled concessions only with public justification
  - Pencil can be used as a small concession if it helps secure unanimous acceptance, but only if it does not undermine Apple or Quill.
  - Jewel can be used as a lever only within a public, auditable Round-2/Round-3 plan that clearly benefits all three and preserves Quill.
5) Suggested public communications (short, clear, auditable)
- Round-4 baseline (default): Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill. Publish pre/post utilities and a 24–48 hour evaluation window for Round-5 Apple-revisit terms.
- Round-3 Apple-revisit pathway (if pursued): Move Jewel to Agent_1; allocations become Agent_1 = Apple + Jewel; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Quill. Publish pre/post utilities; 24–48 hour evaluation, with a concrete Round-5 public plan to finalize Apple revisiting terms.
- If a proposal is blocked, announce a fallback to the stable Round-4 baseline with a tightened Round-5 agenda (public criteria, quick evaluation).
6) Practical next steps I recommend
- Publicly confirm Round-4 Path A as the default baseline to establish a stable, auditable starting point.
- Simultaneously outline a concrete Round-3 Round-5 framework (public and auditable) to revisit Apple, with explicit success criteria and a short decision window.
- If anyone prefers Path B, agree to a precise Round-5 plan up front and insist on Quill’s protection in every step.
If you’d like, I can draft the exact Round-4 public announcement and a compact Round-5 Apple-revisit framework you can post to the thread, plus a simple 1-page evaluation checklist for the 24–48 hour window.

### Raw 98 | category=reflection | phase=reflection_round_4 | round=4 | agent=Agent_2

Here’s a concise, strategist-focused reflection on Round 4 from my perspective as Agent_2, with concrete steps to push toward a real, public consensus in Round 5 while protecting our core interests.
1) What I learned from the proposals and voting outcome
- Round-4 momentum hinges on a stable, auditable baseline that preserves top priorities:
  - Agent_1 wants Apple protected and has a credible path to revisit it later.
  - Agent_2 values Stone + Pencil as a solid, high-utility bundle to keep intact.
  - Agent_3’s non-negotiable is Quill, with Jewel as a potential lever but not at the expense of Quill.
- All three proposals in Round 4 aimed to move toward a simple, auditable state, but none secured unanimous acceptance because Quill’s protection remains a critical sticking point. Any path that loosens Quill is quickly vetoed.
- The core friction isn’t the total value exchanged but the trust that Apple revisits will be credible, public, and beneficial without weakening Quill’s holder.
2) Which participants have compatible vs. conflicting priorities
- Compatible:
  - Agent_1 and Agent_2 share a preference for the clean baseline that preserves Apple with Agent_1 and Stone + Pencil with Agent_2.
  - Agent_3 can accommodate Jewel as a lever, provided Quill stays with Agent_3 and the Apple revisit remains public and credible.
- Conflicting:
  - Any proposal that moves Quill away from Agent_3 (or embeds Jewel in a way that undermines Quill’s security) triggers firm resistance.
  - There is a need for a credible, public, multi-round plan for Apple revisits; without that, agents hesitate to lock in the Round-4 baseline.
3) What seems to be blocking consensus
- Absence of a single, simple, auditable Apple-revisit mechanism that preserves Quill and yields a verifiable net gain for all three.
- Proposals in Round 3/4 tended to bundle multiple shifts, creating two variables to juggle at once rather than a transparent, one-change-at-a-time approach.
- Fear of backsliding: rounds stall when there’s no clear, public assurance about how Apple could be revisited later without risking Quill.
4) Concrete adjustments to move toward consensus (actionable, concrete)
- Lock in a clear Round-4 baseline (public, auditable):
  - Path A as the default: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
  - Publicly publish pre/post utilities and commit to a 24–48 hour evaluation window for any Round-5 Apple-revisit plan.
- Establish a single, public Round-5 Apple-revisit framework (catch-all guardrail):
  - Any Round-5 Apple revisit must be auditable and preserve Quill.
  - Require a measurable net gain for all three (define a simple, public metric, e.g., a delta in total utility that is clearly verifiable).
  - Limit changes to a small, auditable set of reallocations (one or two items at most) to avoid repeat deadlocks.
  - Fix the timeline so a decision is reached within 24–48 hours after the Round-5 proposal is published.
- Enforce a “one-change-at-a-time” discipline for Round-4 proposals:
  - No multi-item swaps in a single Round-4 move. If a change is proposed, it should be just one auditable adjustment that can be judged quickly.
- Build in a clear deadlock-resolution rule:
  - If Round-4 yields no consensus, default to Path A and run a tightly scoped Round-5 Apple-revisit discussion with a concrete, public metric and a strict evaluation window.
- Strengthen messaging to reduce risk perception:
  - Emphasize Quill’s protection as non-negotiable and frame Apple revisits as public, verifiable experiments with quick evaluation windows and a clear path to adjustments.
5) Suggested next-step plan you could publish now
- Round-4 public baseline declaration (default): Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill. Publish pre/post utilities, and commit to a 24–48 hour evaluation window for any Round-5 plan.
- Round-5 Apple-revisit framework (public, auditable): Any Apple-revisit proposal must (a) preserve Quill with Agent_3, (b) deliver a verifiable net gain for all three, (c) present auditable criteria and measurement, (d) involve at most one or two small reallocations, and (e) be evaluated within 24–48 hours.
- If Path B is raised again, require a fully public Round-5 plan with explicit criteria and a tight evaluation window; otherwise revert to the default baseline (Path A) and push the Round-5 framework.
6) Quick, practical language you can use in Round-4 communications
- Round-4 public baseline (default): Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill. Pre/post utilities published; 24–48 hour audit window for Round-5 Apple-revisit terms.
- Round-5 Apple-revisit framework (public): Any proposal must preserve Quill, show a verifiable net gain for all three, and be evaluable within 24–48 hours with at most one or two small reallocations.
- Guardrails: No private side deals; all adjustments public and auditable.
7) Personal stance and suggested posture going forward
- I would lean toward sticking with Path A as the Round-4 baseline to maximize stability and protect Quill, while simultaneously pushing for a crisp, public Round-5 Apple-revisit mechanism with measurable gains.
- If any party pushes Path B, insist on a complete Round-5 plan up front: explicit criteria, a bounded scope (one or two items), public metrics, and a fixed evaluation window before any change is enacted.
If you’d like, I can draft a concise Round-4 public message that codifies Path A as the baseline, plus a ready-to-publish Round-5 Apple-revisit framework text. This would give us a clean, auditable path to move from deadlock toward a real consensus in Round 5.

Reflection on Round 4 outcome and concrete adjustments
What the round taught us
- Quill remains the non-negotiable anchor for Agent_3. Any Round-4 option that moves Quill away from Agent_3 triggers rejection, even if other gains look favorable.
- Agent_1’s Apple remains the most valuable asset in the group for me, but it only has credibility when paired with a public, auditable plan that preserves Quill.
- Agent_2’s Stone + Pencil bundle is the most straightforward, high-utility block for you, and you favor keeping it intact and publicly verifiable.
- The main bottleneck is delivering a credible, public two-step path: a) protect Quill in Round-4, and b) provide a verifiable Round-5 (or Round-3-level) plan that increases total utility without destabilizing Quill.
Compatible vs conflicting priorities
- Compatible
  - Quill with Agent_3 (non-negotiable).
  - Apple with Agent_1 (high value but needs a credible plan to revisit).
  - Stone + Pencil with Agent_2 (clear, stable bundle).
- Conflicting
  - Moves that relocate Quill in Round-4 (they fail immediately unless paired with a credible, public payoff).
  - Over-reliance on private side deals or opaque adjustments for Apple without public metrics.
What’s blocking consensus
- The absence of a simple, public, auditable Round-4 adjustment that keeps Quill with Agent_3 and simultaneously offers a tangible, verifiable gain for the others.
- A lack of a clearly defined, public Round-5 Apple-revisit mechanism that meets three criteria: preserves Quill, yields a net gain for all three, and is evaluated quickly.
Concrete adjustments to move toward consensus
1) Establish a stable Round-4 baseline that protects Quill
- Public baseline (Round-4): Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- Rationale: preserves Quill with Agent_3, keeps Stone+Pencil with Agent_2, and protects Apple with Agent_1. It provides a clean, auditable platform for future rounds.
2) Define a credible, auditable Round-5 Apple-revisit pathway now
- Objective: in Round-5, revisit Apple in a way that is public, auditable, and verifiable, while ensuring Quill remains with Agent_3 in the interim.
- Mechanism (example structure):
  - Move Jewel (or a narrowly scoped adjustment) only if a public, pre-defined gain is demonstrated.
  - Example path (public and auditable): Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1 in Round-5 (Apple+Jewel for Agent_1), with updated totals showing a net gain and a small, fixed evaluation window (24–48 hours).
  - Public criteria for Round-5: Quill remains with Agent_3 in the baseline; everyone sees the before/after utilities; a simple formula shows net gain relative to the Round-4 baseline; a quick 24–48 hour evaluation confirms acceptance or calls for a revised plan.
- Guardrails: if Apple-revisit looks risky or Quill’s security is threatened, revert to a strictly public, alternative adjustment that preserves Quill and yields a verifiable net gain.
3) Public, two-path approach to reduce stalemate
- Path A (default): Round-4 baseline as above; Round-5 Apple revisit via a clean, auditable plan (public criteria, small evaluation window).
- Path B (optional, if objectors exist): A publicly defined, alternative auditable adjustment in Round-5 that preserves Quill and adds a measurable gain, with a parallel evaluation window.
4) Communication and concessions that don’t endanger Quill
- Any concession must be public, small, and tied to a concrete, auditable Round-5 payoff (e.g., a limited Jewel or Pencil move that demonstrably increases total utility without shifting Quill).
- Keep the messaging crisp: baseline reaffirmation, followed by a public Round-5 Apple-revisit framework with explicit metrics and a tight evaluation window.
5) Suggested public framing you can use now
- Round-4 public baseline: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
- Round-5 Apple-revisit framework (public, auditable): If a plan moves forward, move Jewel (or another limited, auditable adjustment) to Agent_1 to increase Apple’s total to 100, with Quill preserved for Agent_3, and a 24–48 hour evaluation to confirm net gains. If accepted, finalize; if not, revert to the baseline with a revised plan.
6) Quick, concrete next steps for you
- Publicly reaffirm Round-4 baseline (Apple with Agent_1; Stone+Pencil with Agent_2; Jewel+Quill with Agent_3) as the standard going into Round-5.
- Invite a concrete, auditable Round-5 Apple-revisit plan now (two clear options: the jewel-to-Apple test or a narrowly-scoped alternative) with:
  - Public pre/post utilities
  - A defined net-gain metric
  - A 24–48 hour evaluation window
  - A simple decision rule for acceptance vs. revision
- Prepare a crisp Round-5 agenda that focuses on the Apple-revisit criteria, keeps Quill safe, and minimizes negotiation friction.

### Raw 121 | category=reflection | phase=reflection_round_5 | round=5 | agent=Agent_1

Here’s a concise, analyst-style reflection and concrete adjustment plan you can use to push toward a round-5 consensus while protecting Apple and Quill.
1) What Round 5 taught us
- Quill is the decisive guardrail. Any proposal that moves Quill away from Agent_3 is likely to be rejected, even if it boosts Apple for Agent_1.
- Proposals that keep Quill with Agent_3 and offer a clear, auditable path to Apple revisiting are the only ones with a realistic chance of broad buy-in.
- Simplicity beats complexity. The group gravitates toward straightforward allocations and public, short evaluation windows (24–48 hours).
2) Compatible vs conflicting priorities
- Compatible:
  - Agent_1 and Agent_2 both prefer clear, high-utility allocations and are open to a public Round-5 Apple-revisit pathway if it’s auditable.
  - Agent_3 will accept Apple-revisit ideas only if Quill remains securely with them.
- Conflicting:
  - Quill’s location and protection is the primary conflict; any plan that jeopardizes Quill triggers broad rejection.
3) What seems to be blocking consensus
- The lack of a single, publicly auditable Round-5 motion that preserves Quill while delivering a credible Apple uplift for Agent_1.
- Proposals in Round 5 moved Quill away from Agent_3, which is a non-starter for Agent_3 and derails consensus.
4) Concrete adjustments to improve consensus (actionable)
- Round-4 baseline (public anchor): Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill. This preserves Quill with Agent_3 and keeps a clean, auditable base.
- Round-5 public path (Plan A, preferred)
  - Move Jewel from Agent_3 to Agent_1; keep Quill with Agent_3.
  - Public allocations for Round-5 would be:
    - Agent_1: Apple + Jewel
    - Agent_2: Stone + Pencil
    - Agent_3: Quill
  - Rationale: Apple rises to 100 for Agent_1; Quill stays with Agent_3; Stone+Pencil remains with Agent_2. Provides a clean, auditable post-state with a clear Round-6 path if needed.
  - Public process: publish pre/post utilities and a 24–48 hour evaluation window. If accepted, finalize Round-5; if not, switch to Plan B.
- Round-5 fallback (Plan B, if Plan A stalls)
  - Allocation: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill
  - Public path: announce a Round-6 Apple-revisit framework with explicit criteria, quick evaluation window, and no risk to Quill in the interim.
  - Guardrails: no private deals; any adjustment must be public and auditable.
- Concessions (only if public and auditable)
  - Pencil: offer as a tiny concession if it helps secure unanimous acceptance and does not undermine Apple or Quill.
  - Jewel: use as a lever only if there’s a credible, public Round-3/Round-5 plan that preserves Apple access in a verifiable way.
- Communication strategy
  - Use a single, clear Round-5 proposal at a time; avoid multi-proposal floodgates.
  - Publish a short, auditable metric (net gain) and a fixed evaluation window (24–48 hours).
  - Emphasize Quill’s protection and the public, verifiable nature of Apple-revisit plans.
5) Ready-to-use Round-5 public message (you can copy/paste)
- Round-5 Plan A (preferred):
  - Jewel moves from Agent_3 to Agent_1; new allocations: Agent_1 = Apple + Jewel; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Quill.
  - Public pre/post utilities posted; 24–48 hour evaluation window to decide acceptance.
  - If accepted, finalize Round-5 as stated and move to a clearly defined Round-6 Apple-revisit framework (auditable, no private deals).
  - If not accepted, revert to Plan B: Round-5 baseline Agent_1 Apple; Agent_2 Stone+Pencil; Agent_3 Jewel+Quill, with a public Round-6 Apple-revisit plan and evaluation window.
- Round-5 Plan B (fallback):
  - Allocation: Agent_1 = Apple; Agent_2 = Stone + Pencil; Agent_3 = Jewel + Quill.
  - Publish a Round-6 Apple-revisit framework up front, with explicit criteria, a quick evaluation window, and public accountability.
6) Short-term next steps
- Publicly reaffirm Round-4 baseline to anchor the discussion.
- Put Plan A forward as the Round-5 public move, with a 24–48 hour audit window. Be explicit that Quill stays with Agent_3.
- If Plan A fails, enact Plan B with a rapid Round-6 Apple-revisit pathway (public and auditable).
- Maintain a strict no-private-deal policy; use a single, simple, auditable metric to evaluate acceptance within the window.

  - Agent_1 and Agent_2 both tend to favor a straightforward baseline that preserves Apple with Agent_1 and keeps Stone + Pencil with Agent_2.
